  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fbc7b469-af85-4d19-9047-63b522f85da6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer11290192100029505898">Ten years ago, Calamity came. It was a burst in the sky that gave ordinary men and women extraordinary powers. The awed public started calling them Epics. But Epics are no friend of man. With incredible gifts came the desire to rule.   <span id="freeText11290192100029505898" style="display:none">Ten years ago, Calamity came. It was a burst in the sky that gave ordinary men and women extraordinary powers. The awed public started calling them Epics. But Epics are no friend of man. With incredible gifts came the desire to rule. And to rule man you must crush his will.<br /><br />Nobody fights the Epics...nobody but the Reckoners. A shadowy group of ordinary humans, they spend their lives studying Epics, finding their weaknesses, and then assassinating them.<br /><br />And David wants in. He wants Steelheart — the Epic who is said to be invincible. The Epic who killed David's father. For years, like the Reckoners, David's been studying, and planning — and he has something they need. Not an object, but an experience.<br /><br />He's seen Steelheart bleed. And he wants revenge.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11290192100029505898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/13474300-nicole"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1456230074i/13474300._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/13474300-nicole">Nicole</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">What a terrible way to approach a book. Let's see -- maybe it's really well written? Or has compelling characters or a gripping plot or any of the oth<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">What a terrible way to approach a book. Let's see -- maybe it's really well written? Or has compelling characters or a gripping plot or any of the other elements that make books good? <br /><br />Just because the subject matter and/or genre "seem" like they've been done before doesn't mean they can't be done well again. That's the challenge that all writers face, after all -- to take a love story or a man v. nature tale and tell it in a fresh and compelling way. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/12166182-shelly-tan"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1415854004i/12166182._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/12166182-shelly-tan">Shelly Tan</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I thought his weakness would be someone who thought of him as a hero, like David's father. That seems so much more interesting than just being feared,<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I thought his weakness would be someone who thought of him as a hero, like David's father. That seems so much more interesting than just being feared, because then you get to play with the idea that Steelheart might've wanted to be a hero but was forced into becoming a villain. That could've tied into how Newcago was supposedly better run than other cities -- an example of Steelheart's efforts to "protect" the people from worse Epic rulers. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550370847?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550370847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4110691812703274948">I got a chance to read an early version of this a little while ago. Needless to say, I jumped at it. <br/><br/>The reason for this is that so far, I haven't read a book by Brandon Sanderson that I haven't loved. That means it's quite likely that I'll get a chance to read another good book, which is always welcome. <br/><br/>OR I'll finally read something of Sanderson's I *don't* like. Which would thrill me, honestly. <br/><br/>Why? Well, because Brandon writes so much faster than me. It only seems fair that some of his stuff</span>
  <span id="freeText4110691812703274948" style="display:none">I got a chance to read an early version of this a little while ago. Needless to say, I jumped at it. <br /><br />The reason for this is that so far, I haven't read a book by Brandon Sanderson that I haven't loved. That means it's quite likely that I'll get a chance to read another good book, which is always welcome. <br /><br />OR I'll finally read something of Sanderson's I *don't* like. Which would thrill me, honestly. <br /><br />Why? Well, because Brandon writes so much faster than me. It only seems fair that some of his stuff should be crap. It just doesn't seem fair that he's brilliant AND fast.... <br /><br />Unfortunately for my ego, Steelheart is another win for Sanderson, proving that he's not a brilliant writer of epic fantasy, he's simply a brilliant writer. Period. <br /><br />Simply said. Great book. Tight writing. Nice take on superheroes. Nice world creation. Absolutely worth your time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4110691812703274948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1002507302" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002507302" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002507302?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17698536-steelheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=superheroes-superhero-like-powers">superheroes-superhero-like-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=diabolical">diabolical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorites-ya">favorites-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorite-secondary-characters">favorite-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=buddy-reads-are-the-best">buddy-reads-are-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002507302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4915934806788255097"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/review-steelheart-by-brandon-sanderson-jessicadhaluska-brandsanderson-randomhousekids.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I'm probably going to make Sandersonite heads everywhere explode when I say this, but STEELHEART might be my new favorite Sanderson book. *does NOT duck* *does NOT run*<br/><br/>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455475838ra/18107305.gif' width='400' height='162' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
<br/><br/>Is it the most beautifully complicated of his works?<br/><br/>No.<br/><br/>Is it the plot-twistiest?<br/><br/>Nope.<br/><br/>Is it the most direct and concise, sans anything that could be construed as meandering?<br/><br/>YAS.<br/><br/>I love Sanderson. Unabashedly. But as someone who's spent a cumulative ten years with my husband, I can state with auth</span>
  <span id="freeText4915934806788255097" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/review-steelheart-by-brandon-sanderson-jessicadhaluska-brandsanderson-randomhousekids.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>I'm probably going to make Sandersonite heads everywhere explode when I say this, but STEELHEART might be my new favorite Sanderson book. *does NOT duck* *does NOT run*<br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455475838ra/18107305.gif" width="400" height="162" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Is it the most beautifully complicated of his works?<br><br>No.<br><br>Is it the plot-twistiest?<br><br>Nope.<br><br>Is it the most direct and concise, sans anything that could be construed as meandering?<br><br>YAS.<br><br>I love Sanderson. Unabashedly. But as someone who's spent a cumulative ten years with my husband, I can state with authority that 'love' does not mean 'blind to flaws.' #sorrynotsorry<br><br>And this was just FUN. Which was exactly what I needed after my last several books (I'm looking at you, <b>
  <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/early-review-morning-star-by-pierce-brown-jessicadhaluska-delreybooks-pierce_brown-sonsofares_.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Morning Star</a>
</b>).<br><br>Meet David. <br><br>David is an orphan who's father was killed in front of him by an Epic (humans who began to manifest superhero-like powers after Calamity appeared in the sky--no, we don't know what Calamity is, but it might be my new favorite curse word) named Steelheart when he was a child. *squints* Okay, so it wasn't 100% flowers and rainbows, but beyond the sad backgrounds of several of our characters, it was frequently hilarious.<br><br>David and his terrible metaphors are the source of most of the hilarity:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I stopped as I noticed something different. Motorcycles. <br>There were three of them in a row near the far side of the hallway. I hadn’t seen them at first, as I’d been focused on the guns. They were sleek, their bodies a deep green with black patterns running up their sides. They made me want to hunch over and crouch down to make myself have less wind resistance. I could imagine shooting through the streets on one of these. <b>They looked so dangerous, like alligators. Really fast alligators wearing black. Ninja alligators.</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Ninja alligators. *giggle snorts*<br><br>But David isn't a one man show, there's also the rest of the team:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“Don’t you </i>ever<i> pay attention?” Tia asked. “We’ve talked about this.”<br>“He was cleaning his guns,” Abraham said.<br>“I’m an artist,” Cody said.<br>Abraham nodded. “He’s an artist.”<br><b>“And cleanliness is next to deadliness,” Cody added.</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Then there's the genius that is Sanderson. Part of the reason I loved STEELHEART was how much easier it was to backtrack the groundwork of his LIES. <br><br>See, Sanderson doesn't limit himself to unobtrusively weaving hints about future reveals. No, no . . . He <i>deliberately</i> leads you astray. Sometimes in numerous ways. <br><br><i>Sometimes</i> he paints a clear picture in the very beginning, but then so skillfully undermines the idea that YOU LAUGH AT YOURSELF for having such silly thoughts. <br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392066518ra/8495145.gif" width="245" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>In 1000+ pages of these machinations, it's impossible to look back and see where you went wrong. The best you can hope for is to find <i>some</i> of your missteps, while you throw heavy objects b/c you know, YOU KNOW, it said something about such-and-such-somewhere (&lt;------does NOT make for good document searches), but you'll NEVER find it. <br><br>In less than 400 pages? Easy peasy.<br><br>I am learning the darks paths of your mind, Sanderson. I will not remain your puppet forever. <br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455475838i/18107306.jpg" width="300" height="395" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>SO. Do you like supervillains? Do you like adorkable manboys who will not stand back and let evil triumph? Do you like NEVER being able to guess ALL THE THINGS an author has in store for you? Then you, friend, should give STEELHEART by Brandon Sanderson a try. It is fantastic. Highly recommended. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Pre-review, part, the second:</b><br><br>WELL . . . That was equal parts spectacular and exhausting (b/c FEELS). I was a bit worried, b/c I thought MISTBORN #2 was OTT teen-angsty, and it wasn't even YA, so what would deliberate YA from Sanderson look like?<br><br>Perfection, that's what. Near perfection, anyway.<br><br>And I'm not just saying that b/c I . . . GUESSED THE MAIN PLOT TWIST!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454981206ra/18036888.gif" width="400" height="183" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1542693296" rel="nofollow noopener">Mitosis (The Reckoners, #1.5)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1549043851" rel="nofollow noopener">Firefight (The Reckoners, #2)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/971640844" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity (The Reckoners, #3)</a>
</b></span>

<div id="review_783187045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/783187045" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/783187045?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781299859296" href="/book/show/15704458-steelheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer783187045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13170910042819333765"><b>Well... that was disappointing.</b><br/><br/>I've heard such great things about all of Brandon Sanderson's books and he's an author I've been meaning to read for what seems like forever. So I decided to pick up his recent young adult work instead of committing to a series with several releases already... well, all I can say is that I hope this isn't representative of all his books because <i>Steelheart</i> really disappointed me. In my opinion, there is nothing you can get from this book that you can't get from bett</span>
  <span id="freeText13170910042819333765" style="display:none"><b>Well... that was disappointing.</b><br><br>I've heard such great things about all of Brandon Sanderson's books and he's an author I've been meaning to read for what seems like forever. So I decided to pick up his recent young adult work instead of committing to a series with several releases already... well, all I can say is that I hope this isn't representative of all his books because <i>Steelheart</i> really disappointed me. In my opinion, there is nothing you can get from this book that you can't get from better books about superheroes and supervillains like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious" title="Vicious by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2536134.Gone__Gone___1_" title="Gone (Gone, #1) by Michael Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone</a>. Unless, of course, you are specifically looking for cliched characters, predictable twists and tiresome descriptions of weaponry.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396660055ra/9168949.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>It was just very meh.</u>
</b><br><br>Sanderson seems to be a competent writer and he starts by setting the opening scene very well. It's dramatic, people die, we get a feel for why David wants vengeance - all good. The story isn't a new idea, it's about certain people (called "Epics") developing superpowers and using those powers to terrorize others and build empires based on fear. Then, among all of this, a group of rebels form to try and take down the Epics one by one and reclaim the world they once knew (these people are called the Reckoners). David seeks to join the Reckoners because he has valuable knowledge that could be the key to bringing down Steelheart - and that is what David wants most of all. <br><br><b>I personally feel like this is a book written by a man for other men.</b> Or boys. Whatever. I've been lectured for calling various novels "boy books" in the past - I tend to get female readers angrily pounding their chests and asking how dare I suggest that women don't want to read about cars and guns and whatnot. And, let me be clear, <b>they were completely right</b>. They had every right to be annoyed that I'd used the term so carelessly - and offensively - without fully explaining what I mean. Because I do see myself as a feminist and don't feel like men and women have to read certain types of books that suit their gender. I feel lucky to have a brother who read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_" title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> (and liked it) because I recommended it ^_^<br><br><b>But...</b><br><br>There are books like this that feel specifically catered towards straight male readers. Which I guess may not be a bad thing if you are a straight male reader, but as I am not, I struggled to like it. For one thing, <b>there are hardly any women in this book</b>. Almost all of the big Epics with the snazziest powers are male. There is one central female character called Megan (two if you count Tia, but I don't) and her characterization consists entirely of what a fine piece of ass David thinks she is. <br><br>Of course, many women will still enjoy (and have enjoyed) this book, just as many women enjoy the old James Bond films. But there's something about cardboard cutouts of male wish fulfillment - a hero who is so damn perfect, intelligent, and has all the best toys; hot ladies; and cartoon-y Good vs Evil type characters - that just never appeals to me. You can get superheroes, science and fast-paced action scenes in books like <i>
  <b>Gone</b>
</i> by Michael Grant, but with more detailed, complex characters that don't feel like stereotypes. You can get a far more sophisticated exploration of Good vs Evil in <i>
  <b>Vicious</b>
</i> by Victoria Schwab. I would recommend either of those over this.<br><br>*sigh* Maybe Mr Sanderson just isn't for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13170910042819333765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1246080900" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1246080900" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1246080900?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246080900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2636993053503955120"><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>So I'm going to start out by saying the only reason I docked half a star is because I felt the pacing of this story was a little uneven. <b>It was not detrimental,</b> but the most interesting portion of the plot unfolded quickly right at the end of the book & it was <u>just a little</u> off balance from the rest of the story.<br/><br/><b>Otherwise, this is one hell of a book!</b><br/><br/>After the world is visited by Calamity, average humans are randomly gifted supernatural powers. These humans are called Epic</span>
  <span id="freeText2636993053503955120" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />So I'm going to start out by saying the only reason I docked half a star is because I felt the pacing of this story was a little uneven. <b>It was not detrimental,</b> but the most interesting portion of the plot unfolded quickly right at the end of the book &amp; it was <u>just a little</u> off balance from the rest of the story.<br /><br /><b>Otherwise, this is one hell of a book!</b><br /><br />After the world is visited by Calamity, average humans are randomly gifted supernatural powers. These humans are called Epics, <b>and they are not the heroes everyone hoped they would be.</b><br /><br />Following a tragic incident, the last ten years of David's life has revolved around researching the strengths &amp; weaknesses of these extraordinary people. When he discovers an opportunity to join an anti-Epic rebel group, David sees his chance for revenge is closer than he thought possible.<br /><br /><b>This is how Young Adult stories should be written.</b><br /><br />David is capable &amp; talented in a realistic way. He's smarter than average teenager, but has a tendency to shoot from the hip &amp; fixates on small scale goals instead of seeing the bigger picture. <br /><br /><i>David does not suffer from Gary Stu-syndrome.</i> Which is <b>refreshing</b> to say the least. His abilities &amp; dialogue are reflective of his age without feeling too juvenile. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart__Reckoners___1_" title="Steelheart (Reckoners, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a> presents the reader with a classic good vs. evil story on its surface, but as layers of the plot are revealed it becomes <b>much more than that.</b><br /><br />It's fast-paced &amp; full of exciting action! This book invites the reader to speculate along with the characters about how to solve the problems the Epics present. <br /><br />The technology &amp; world Sanderson creates here is unique &amp; satisfying to read about. There were twists I guessed &amp; twists &amp; didn't so it's safe to say <b>I had fun the entire time.</b><br /><br />I always enjoy when books <b>rely heavily on logical reasoning</b> instead of drawing out the characters into <b>unrealistic &amp; often contrived situations</b> just to create drama. <u>You'll find none of that nonsense here.</u><br /><br />Sanderson is a master storyteller &amp; it really becomes apparent in how <b>consistently well</b> he writes across many genres. I am shamelessly in love with <b>just about everything he writes.</b> If an action-packed, Science Fiction superhero story turned on its head sounds up your alley, I <u>would not hesitate</u> to give this book a try!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2636993053503955120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer738042671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11978434648687669232"><b>Kindle deal for a limited time for $1.99 11Apr20 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Steelheart-Reckoners-Book-Brandon-Sanderson-ebook/dp/B00ARHAAZ6/ref=sr_1_78?dchild=1&qid=1586615764&s=digital-text&sr=1-78' rel='nofollow noopener'>at Amazon</a></b><br/><br/><b>3rd Read</b> with by favorite buddy reading group <a>Buddies Books & Baubles</a><br/><br/><b>Why should you read this series in a nut shell:</b><br/><br/>❶ - David is the most <b>Adorkable</b> <i>yes it is a real word</i> character I've ever read. <br/><br/>❷ - There are EVIL superheroes. <b>EVIL SUPERHEROES!!!</b><br/><br/>❸ - Lots of different kinds of action happening. Motorcycle chases, car crashes, one on on fighting...etc<br/><br/>❹ - A really good twist (actually about 3 but they were all awesome) and I only semi guess</span>
  <span id="freeText11978434648687669232" style="display:none"><b>Kindle deal for a limited time for $1.99 11Apr20 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Steelheart-Reckoners-Book-Brandon-Sanderson-ebook/dp/B00ARHAAZ6/ref=sr_1_78?dchild=1&amp;qid=1586615764&amp;s=digital-text&amp;sr=1-78" rel="nofollow noopener">at Amazon</a></b><br><br><b>3rd Read</b> with by favorite buddy reading group <a>Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a><br><br><b>Why should you read this series in a nut shell:</b><br><br>❶ - David is the most <b>Adorkable</b> <i>yes it is a real word</i> character I've ever read. <br><br>❷ - There are EVIL superheroes. <b>EVIL SUPERHEROES!!!</b><br><br>❸ - Lots of different kinds of action happening. Motorcycle chases, car crashes, one on on fighting...etc<br><br>❹ - A really good twist (actually about 3 but they were all awesome) and I only semi guessed a smidgen of one of them.<br><br>❺ - BAD METAPHORS.....look they are so bad they are good. Like great or at least super funny.<br><br><br>2nd read:<br><br><b>Buddy Read/Reread TODAY Dec 8 2014 with my fellow Sandersonitus Sufferers <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer" rel="nofollow noopener">Athena (Shardbearer)</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5600230-armina" rel="nofollow noopener">Armina</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8192509-gavin" rel="nofollow noopener">Gavin</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/21830787-kat-stark" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat Stark</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136" rel="nofollow noopener">Evengy</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12571107-desinka" rel="nofollow noopener">Desinka</a>, <a>Alexa</a>, <a>Shandra</a>, <a>Annette</a>, <a>Nicholas</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5892196-carole-s-random-life" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole</a>, <a>Ashley</a>, <a href="%E2%80%9D" rel="nofollow noopener">Eon</a>, <a>Kristen</a>, <a>Danae</a> and we also hijacked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-oosarahoo" rel="nofollow noopener">oOSarahOo</a> Last Minute.<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/steelheartquote_zpsa054b24f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417988220i/12632643.jpg" alt=" photo steelheartquote_zpsa054b24f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br><br>On the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2097427-steelheart-1-of-reckoners-series" rel="nofollow noopener">Reckoners Group Read Thread</a></b> <br><br><b>Original Review October 2013:</b><br><br>Imagine a world where there are no good X-Men. What would happen if there are only villains with great powers and no heroes? What becomes of the cities, government, people in general? That is what Steelheart is about. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I know, better than anyone else, that there are no heroes coming to save us. There are no good Epics. None of them protect us. Power corrupts, and absolute power corrupts absolutely.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>David learned that at a young age the first time he saw Steelheart, the day his father died. Since then he has lived his life with one goal and one goal only. To kill the Epic that killed his father.<br><br>This is my very first Brandon Sanderson novel and I loved it. Sometimes it is difficult for me to read UF from a male perspective it ends up being all about big boobs and girls in skin tight clothing and high heeled boots but that couldn’t be farther from the truth here. Brandon created a very intricate dystopian world in the wreckage of Chicago now referred to as Newcago. He has painstakingly thought out a class system for all of the Epics and the powers they use. He has also built a believable resistance of renegade humans that try to fight against them. I was definitely impressed with the sheer volume of thought that went into those two items of the story.<br><br>I was interested in this world from the beginning. David is a very likeable character he is a slight know it all but has the hardest time putting a metaphor together which kind of made him endearing to me. Once he meets up with the Renegades you can tell he really has been alone for most of his life and protector that I am I just wants him to win. Of course there is an older man to look up to has a substitute father figure that helps guide our young David out of his blind hate and need for revenge.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “It’s good for you to think of this, son. Ponder. Worry. Stay up nights, frightened for the casualties of your ideology. It will do you good to realize the price of fighting”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There are some really nice philosophical questions posed that can make this more than just a story of revenge. You have the choice to delve in and think of this world on a deeper level or just move on with the story. No agenda is forced on you which I appreciate as a reader.<br><br>There is a cute little crush romance that isn’t quite insta love but is heartwarming all the same and some very interesting developments that I really didn’t see coming. The story twisted just enough at the end that I really was surprised. I seriously had a moment of woe is that real.<br><br>Actionwise sometimes it is over the top for me (I’m a girl but my stepson disagrees with my assessment whole heartedly). It is an action book for sure and there are a lot of scenes with fighting and motorcycle chases and a final battle that goes on for multiple chapters. <br><br>All in all good storlyline, nice pacing, solid world building for a first book of a series and great start to the layering that I see will come out in future books in the series. All of the characters definitely have a backstory worth developing a little more.<br><br>I will definitely have to check out some of Mr. Sanderson’s other works if they compare to or are better than this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11978434648687669232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1004952257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004952257" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004952257?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=super-heroes">super-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004952257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer847702285001339654"><b>
  <i>I've seen Steelheart bleed.</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>I always love when a book begins with a solid first sentence. And this novel was a good example of that.<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>PUSHED TO THE NEXT STEP OF EVOLUTION</u>
</b><br/><br/>This is my first book by Brandon Sanderson and now I realize why he is so popular and well rated by a lot of readers and reviewers. Certainly he has a great style and entertaining style that you aren't never bored of what is happening. I am aware that this novel is from a genre kinda new to him since this is a "super-hero" </span>
  <span id="freeText847702285001339654" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>I've seen Steelheart bleed.</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />I always love when a book begins with a solid first sentence. And this novel was a good example of that.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>PUSHED TO THE NEXT STEP OF EVOLUTION</u>
</b><br /><br />This is my first book by Brandon Sanderson and now I realize why he is so popular and well rated by a lot of readers and reviewers. Certainly he has a great style and entertaining style that you aren't never bored of what is happening. I am aware that this novel is from a genre kinda new to him since this is a "super-hero" book while he has been writing more in the genres of epic fantasy. However, I wanted to try this author on this particular novel since I am huge fan of super-heroes and since this was a prose novel in that genre, well, I supposed that it was a good way to know if I'd like this author. Well, the test was successful, I loved the book and I am a fan of him already.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Where there are villains, there will be heroes.</i>
</b><br /><br />It's quite awesome the setting of this book series, where an astronomic phenomenon known as "Calamity" appeared on the orbit of planet Earth and due unexplicable reasons, several people at random got super-powers, and all of them became evil!!! They are known as "Epics" and now they ruled the world with iron fist, controlling cities and making havok. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Sometimes...you have to help the heroes along.</i>
</b><br /><br />A kid loses his father in the cruel hands of an Epic and he chooses to dedicate his life to find a way to kill that Epic, and now a young adult, his plans need to get associated to an underground secret group known as "The Reckoners" formed by normal humans risking their lives to kill as many Epics as possible to free humanity from this villanious menace.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The way the world was these days, you did what you had to in order to survive.</i>
</b><br /><br />The United States Federal Government collapsed due the Epics' attacks and now those lands are known as the "Fractured States", where very little cities are functional yet, and one of those is Chicago that later that an Epic known as "Steelheart" got control over the city, now it's known as Newcago (that honestly, when this book would be translated to Spanish, I don't know how smart would be to keep that name since "cago" is the Spanish for "to shit" sort of, that in Chicago, I supposed that one is used to the name and didn't make the association but in Newcago, well, whenever I read the name of the city, I can't avoid to smile a bit.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>POWER CORRUPTS...</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>I sometimes wonder if they came along because we thought we could explain everything.</i>
</b><br /><br />These Epics have amazing powers whom defy physics such as one epic able to fire a gun and never being out of bullets. So, anything is possible. However, the key thing here is that each epic has a weakness. So, finding out his/her weakness is the key to be able to beat them and kill them. However, in the same way that the powers aren't limited to the realm of physics, the weakenesses can be anything, and many times finding out can be an almost impossible task.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>You've got passion to kill, but you need to find passion to live.</i>
</b><br /><br />The idea of evil super-humans isn't new, since on the process of the creation of "Superman", the first super-hero in literature, he was conceived first as a super-villain, but since his creators got trouble to get somebody to publish their work, during the struggles of keep looking for a publishing house, they came out with the twist of making "Superman" as a hero... a super-hero!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>What is it to be King if you have nobody to follow you?</i>
</b><br /><br />The young man who wishes to kill Steelheart is named David, David Charleston, and I think that it was a great idea to name him like that since he is a "David" trying to kill "Goliaths" with super-powers. And Steelheart is one of the most powerful ones ever existed, with super-strenght, flight, energy bolts, steel-converting fields and invulnerability and no respect for any human being. Along with his fantastic collection of powers, he is supported by a select team of Epics, and also an Enforcement army of soldiers ruling the city of Newcago.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Adding a new team member always upends the dynamic.</i>
</b><br /><br />David will join The Reckoners with a bold plan... to kill Steelheart. David seen Steelheart bleed once, so, he knows that it's possible to kill Steelheart, but knowing the concept and finding out what the heck is the real weakness of Steelheart is another thing. David is the new member of The Reckoners and he is changing the dynamic of the team, however, is that is a good thing is too soon to be certain.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Don't act because you can, act because it's the right thing to do.</i>
</b><br /><br />Even there will be many doubts about killing Steelheart or not. He is evil sure, however, Newcago is one of the very few cities able to hold people with basic needs like electricity, water, food, jobs. Don't be mistaken, Steelheart demands blind obedience to any citizen in Newcago, but definitely that's quite better to the situation in other cities where other Epics just destroyed the towns. So, even if they would be in the position to kill Steelheart... is it the wise movement to do in this very risky chessgame where the humanity is now trapped. How far The Reckoners can go without becoming terrorists instead of freedom fighters?<br /><br /><b>
  <i>What terrorist didn't think he or she was the good guy?</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>Steelheart</i> is just the first novel and I have no doubt that this book series will getting better and better!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="847702285001339654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2369668365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2369668365" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2369668365?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369668365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9169355309793904172"><b>What if Superman was evil?</b><br/>In fact, what if <i>all</i> superpowered beings were evil? <--and <i>that's</i> the premise of this book.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525447398ra/25481174.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>So. If (for unknown reasons) there were suddenly people granted superpowers, and (for unknown reasons) they all turned into bad guys, and they all (for unknown reasons) had secret strange weaknesses that made no sense - then who would fight them?<br/><b>Enter the Reckoners!</b><br/>A bunch of humans who ferret out the weakness and then kill the Epic. <--Epic is what these powered people are refer</span>
  <span id="freeText9169355309793904172" style="display:none"><b>What if Superman was evil?</b><br>In fact, what if <i>all</i> superpowered beings were evil? &lt;--and <i>that's</i> the premise of this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525447398ra/25481174.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So. If (for unknown reasons) there were suddenly people granted superpowers, and (for unknown reasons) they all turned into bad guys, and they all (for unknown reasons) had secret strange weaknesses that made no sense - then who would fight them?<br><b>Enter the Reckoners!</b><br>A bunch of humans who ferret out the weakness and then kill the Epic. &lt;--Epic is what these powered people are referred to as, btw.<br>Basically, these Reckoners are just the Great Value version of Batman.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525447398ra/25481175.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Alright, so society has been destroyed by the Epics, and there's no point (and in most cases, no <i>way</i>) for the puny humans to fight back. <br>David lives in this city (used to be Chicago) that's run by one of the most powerful Epics out there, Steelheart, and he dreams of bringing him down because Steelheart killed his father.<br><b>AND ON THAT DAY, DAVID SAW HIM BLEED!</b> &lt;--this is important<br>As in, the whole book is about David joining the Reckoners and convincing them that somewhere in his memory is the key to Steelheart's secret weakness. <br>So they can finally... <br><b>Take. Him. Down.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525449325ra/25481297.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Amidst the plotting, hiding, and fighting there's an awkward love story thrown in with this girl named Megan. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It really annoyed me that it was incredibly obvious almost from the first that she was an Epic, but that it was played out like it was some BIG REVEAL at the end. Dude, seriously? Even her 'death' wasn't convincing! I was facepalming so hard by the time she was in the tunnels as the <i>'illusion'</i> he was facing that I dented my head a bit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br>Why did he even like her? She was an asssssshole. I get it, she was a hot asshole. But still! I wasn't exactly a fan.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506812868ra/24055909.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Ok, this was a pretty easy-breezy read so I don't want anyone to think I hated it, I just don't think I read the same book everyone else did. I simply didn't find David or his problems making <i>metaphors</i> endearing, I didn't care for the romance, and I didn't find the twists very twisty.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Of <b>course</b> the leader-dude was an Epic! How did they not see that?! Or at the very least, become suspicious?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>BUT.</b><br>I was able to scarf it down quickly and didn't find it some chore to slog through. I don't think I'll continue with the series, though.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9169355309793904172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_633995310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633995310" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633995310?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781299859296" href="/book/show/15704458-steelheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633995310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14694175188066779553">This book = insanity!<br/><br/>This will prove my living under a rock, but I had not heard of this author before I went to Book Expo and got told all about his awesome status, and let me tell you, the praise is not unwarranted! Steelheart does not hold back; it's an edge-of-your-seat read with an intensity that requires you to put the book down regularly just so you can take a breather!<br/><br/>There are book beginnings... then there are Sanderson beginnings; the prologue is all it took to make me fall in love wit</span>
  <span id="freeText14694175188066779553" style="display:none">This book = insanity!<br><br>This will prove my living under a rock, but I had not heard of this author before I went to Book Expo and got told all about his awesome status, and let me tell you, the praise is not unwarranted! Steelheart does not hold back; it's an edge-of-your-seat read with an intensity that requires you to put the book down regularly just so you can take a breather!<br><br>There are book beginnings... then there are Sanderson beginnings; the prologue is all it took to make me fall in love with this book. Already, my heart was pounding, I was left gasping, and my knuckles were white from clutching the book. Sanderson's writing brought me thoroughly and completely in David's world - a very dark, merciless world - and in it I stayed until the last page was turned! My advice to you: buckle up, because it's a wild, turbulent ride!<br><br>In David's world, the Epics - humans with extraordinary powers - have taken over. You must abide by their rules to survive and then hope you go unnoticed. This may not sound like anything new - your average comic book premise, even - but the creativity is in the details. The world building does not falter; with every turn of a page the world comes alive with devastatingly grim, yet strangely picturesque, details. Sanderson paints this cinematic picture of a world corrupted by power. Each new Epic introduced is more fascinating than the last, not to mention terrifying. The various powers that range from death by command, to illusionists, to controlling daylight, coupled with the concept of weaknesses, are imaginative and utterly compelling. Much like Calamity which remains the enigma behind it all, yet to be explored but full of promise. This all results in an unpredictable plot with no limits or hesitations. Not once did I know what was coming next, though I learned quickly to not let myself relax for even a second. <br><br>Now let's meet the characters. We have a protagonist who's dedicated his life to learning about the Epics, his knowledge on the matter turns him into a capable and intelligent character. His awkwardness around a certain girl and his terrible analogies offer some comic relief to the story's borderline unbearable tension while carving him into a flawed, easily relatable character. He soon teams up with the Reckoners, a group who is fighting back against the Epics. Each member of this team brings forth a memorable personality, and a few have an air of mystery that will make you constantly question everything about their character. The powerhouse in this book, however, is none other than Steelheart himself. He makes his presence known during the first few pages, paralyzing us with his sheer power, ruthlessness, and invincibility. Most of the plot - especially its mystery - is spent on figuring out what exactly could lead to his defeat, but finding this weakness feels like an insurmountable challenge. My imagination was running rampant with infinite theories and possibilities that made it all the more riveting. Even though I was on the right track, I found myself reveling in the brilliance that was this ending! Besides, this book is so wildly action packed with wicked fight scenes that are so vicious and intense, that you won't care to spend much time predicting anything at all, let alone achieve success with idle guesses. <br><br>Do yourself a favor and get yourself a copy of this book! Steelheart is a spectacular read that's impossible to put down; sit comfortably, take a (deep) breath, now get ready to be up all night!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14694175188066779553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1172720604" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1172720604?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18245330-steelheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1172720604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13305786010255133896"><i>
  <b>“I’ve seen Steelheart bleed. And I will see him bleed again.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Epics are humans with super powers. These powers corrupt their souls, turning them into tyrannical murderers that think themselves divine. <br/><br/>Steelheart is one of these and he has the ability to turn anything he touches into steel, including his own skin which renders him completely impervious to harm. He murdered David’s father, but not before he managed to shoot him in the face leaving a scar on the supposedly invincible Epic’s chee</span>
  <span id="freeText13305786010255133896" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“I’ve seen Steelheart bleed. And I will see him bleed again.”</b>
</i><br><br>Epics are humans with super powers. These powers corrupt their souls, turning them into tyrannical murderers that think themselves divine. <br><br>Steelheart is one of these and he has the ability to turn anything he touches into steel, including his own skin which renders him completely impervious to harm. He murdered David’s father, but not before he managed to shoot him in the face leaving a scar on the supposedly invincible Epic’s cheek. David is the only person to ever see him bleed, and has spent the rest of his life planning to make him do it again. A task easier said than done it seems. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1421695365p8/1124632.jpg" width="400" height="322" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>David, now eighteen, wants to join the Reckoners: a select group of Epic hunters. They’re highly skilled and kitted out with marvellous technology. The technology was invented by their founder, Prof, and grants them shielding and disintegration abilities. David believes with their help he can kill his nemesis. The only problem is they’re surviving by using covert ops, so finding them is a little bit tricky. And getting them to trust you is even harder. <br><br>The Reckoners are quite an eccentric group of characters. Prof’s everyday clothing is a lab coat dyed black. The using of his own tech changes his mood so much that his personality is altered entirely. At least, that’s how David sees it in the beginning. The revelation on why this happens is quite a shocker. The rest of the group are quite an eclectic cast as well. In the midst of them David even finds a love interest, though she doesn’t seem to like him back. He doesn’t quite understand why, until the very end when Sanderson throws yet another shocker at us.<br><br><b>A revenge mission layered with lots of action and blood </b><br><br>Every Epic has a weakness, each one is more random and bizarre than the last. Steelheart’s weakness has only manifested itself once, when David’s father shot him, and it’s almost impossible to tell what that weakness was: it could have been anything in the room at the time. It could have been a simple thought or even an emotion. David is determined to discover what it is. However, Steelheart has proclaimed himself Emperor of Newcago and consequently has a host of lesser Epics at his disposal. Nightwielder is incorporeal and can shape shadows into spears. Firefight is a wielder of flame and Conflux is literally a human battery. Each one is a servant to Steelheart’s evil rule. Getting to him won't be easy. <br><br>David and the Reckoners have a lot to go through if they wish to bring down Steelheart. And the author has crammed it all into four-hundred pages of fast writing that opens up this series in a great way. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1421696882p8/1124645.jpg" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13305786010255133896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1575276873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575276873" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Sagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53505099-elizabeth-sagan"><img alt="Elizabeth Sagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527068343p2/53505099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1575276873?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Sagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Sagan" href="/user/show/53505099-elizabeth-sagan">Elizabeth Sagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575276873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer644711120812293294">My relationship with The Reckoners series is like a relationship with someone you love deeply, despite the fact that they cheated on you and they’re chewing out loud (we all know that is a deal breaker). In other words, I adore the idea of this series so much that I can partially ignore the fact that it’s not that amazingly written. Brandon Sanderson is one of my favourite authors and I’m kinda disappointed that he chose such a light tone on this one when I know, I know, I KNOW he could’ve creat</span>
  <span id="freeText644711120812293294" style="display:none">My relationship with The Reckoners series is like a relationship with someone you love deeply, despite the fact that they cheated on you and they’re chewing out loud (we all know that is a deal breaker). In other words, I adore the idea of this series so much that I can partially ignore the fact that it’s not that amazingly written. Brandon Sanderson is one of my favourite authors and I’m kinda disappointed that he chose such a light tone on this one when I know, I know, I KNOW he could’ve created a masterpiece, if only he would’ve treated it like he treated The Mistborn series.<br /><br />The action is set in our world, but some people (called Epics and what a cool name that is) have supernatural powers AND THEY’RE USING THEM FOR THEIR OWN BENEFIT! This last part is the reason I’m madly in love with this series, even if it doesn’t deserve it. But when you’re fed up with stories about “the greater good” and “great power comes with great responsibility”, something like that comes like a breth of fresh air.<br /><br />But please, please, please, don’t turn this into a book for kids, especially when I know what you’re capable of writing. This story had so much potential. I would’ve loved to learn more about Steelheart himself. Or about other Epics. Or about their rise to power. Every time Steelheart was mentioned I felt like I was given one spoon of water to keep me alive, just enough so I can continue reading.<br /><br />In addition, compared to, let’s say, Vin from the Mistborn series, the characters were so plain. I know the book isn’t that big and you don’t have that much space to develop them, but... ***insert disappointed sigh***.<br /><br />I had high expectations from this novel and it could’ve easily become the best book/series I’ve ever read. But it was too... too YA. Too soft. Still, I will rate it 5 stars for it’s main theme alone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="644711120812293294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
